<th scope="row">Website</th>
<td><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.mcgm.gov.in">www<wbr />.mcgm<wbr />.gov<wbr />.in</a></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Mumbai</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ʊ/ short 'oo' in 'foot'">ʊ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/aɪ/ long 'i' in 'tide'">aɪ</span></span>/</a></span></span>; also known as <b>Bombay</b>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_renamed_Indian_cities_and_states#Maharashtra" title="List of renamed Indian cities and states">the official name until 1995</a>) is the <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital city</a> of the <a href="/wiki/States_and_Territories_of_India" class="mw-redirect" title="States and Territories of India">Indian state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Maharashtra" title="Maharashtra">Maharashtra</a>. It is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_most_populous_cities_in_India" class="mw-redirect" title="List of most populous cities in India">most populous city in India</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_agglomerations_by_population" title="List of agglomerations by population">ninth most populous agglomeration in the world</a>, with an estimated city population of 18.4&#160;million. Along with the neighbouring regions of the <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_Metropolitan_Region" title="Mumbai Metropolitan Region">Mumbai Metropolitan Region</a>, it is one of the most populous <a href="/wiki/List_of_urban_agglomerations_by_population" class="mw-redirect" title="List of urban agglomerations by population">urban regions</a> in the world and the second most populous <a href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_in_India" title="List of metropolitan areas in India">metropolitan area</a> in India, with a population of 20.7&#160;million as of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mumbai&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-pibmumbai_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pibmumbai-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Mumbai lies on the <a href="/wiki/Konkan" title="Konkan">west coast of India</a> and has a deep natural harbour. In 2009, Mumbai was named an <a href="/wiki/Alpha_world_city" class="mw-redirect" title="Alpha world city">alpha world city</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> It is also the wealthiest city in India,<sup id="cite_ref-livemint.com_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-livemint.com-13">[13]</a></sup> and has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_by_GDP#Asia.2C_Central_.26_South" title="List of cities by GDP">highest GDP</a> of any city in <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Asia" class="mw-redirect" title="West Asia">West</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Mumbai has the highest number of <a href="/wiki/Billionaires" class="mw-redirect" title="Billionaires">billionaires</a> and <a href="/wiki/Millionaires" class="mw-redirect" title="Millionaires">millionaires</a> among all cities in India.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Seven_islands_of_Bombay" class="mw-redirect" title="Seven islands of Bombay">seven islands</a> that came to constitute Mumbai were home to communities of <a href="/wiki/Kolis" class="mw-redirect" title="Kolis">fishing colonies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nirc.nanzan-u.ac.jp_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nirc.nanzan-u.ac.jp-4">[4]</a></sup> For centuries, the islands were under the control of successive <a href="/wiki/History_of_Mumbai_under_indigenous_empires" title="History of Mumbai under indigenous empires">indigenous empires</a> before being <a href="/wiki/Ceded" class="mw-redirect" title="Ceded">ceded</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese</a> and subsequently to the <a href="/wiki/British_East_India_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="British East India Company">British East India Company</a> when in 1661 <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">King Charles II</a> married the Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Catherine_of_Braganza" title="Catherine of Braganza">Catherine of Braganza</a>, and as part of her dowry Charles received the ports of <a href="/wiki/Tangier" title="Tangier">Tangier</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seven_islands_of_Bombay" class="mw-redirect" title="Seven islands of Bombay">seven islands of Bombay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> During the mid-18th century, Bombay was reshaped by the <a href="/wiki/Hornby_Vellard" title="Hornby Vellard">Hornby Vellard</a> project,<sup id="cite_ref-Dwivedi_2001_28_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dwivedi_2001_28-18">[18]</a></sup> which undertook reclamation of the area between the seven islands from the sea.<sup id="cite_ref-fp-onceuponatime_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fp-onceuponatime-19">[19]</a></sup> Along with construction of major roads and railways, the reclamation project, completed in 1845, transformed Bombay into a major seaport on the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Sea" title="Arabian Sea">Arabian Sea</a>. Bombay in the 19th century was characterised by economic and educational development. During the early 20th century it became a strong base for the <a href="/wiki/Indian_independence_movement" title="Indian independence movement">Indian independence movement</a>. Upon India's independence in 1947 the city was incorporated into <a href="/wiki/Bombay_State" title="Bombay State">Bombay State</a>. In 1960, following the <a href="/wiki/Samyukta_Maharashtra_Samiti" class="mw-redirect" title="Samyukta Maharashtra Samiti">Samyukta Maharashtra movement</a>, a new state of <a href="/wiki/Maharashtra" title="Maharashtra">Maharashtra</a> was created with Bombay as the capital.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mumbai is the <a href="/wiki/Financial_centre" title="Financial centre">financial</a>, commercial<sup id="cite_ref-millionaireRoleModel_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-millionaireRoleModel-21">[21]</a></sup> and entertainment capital of India. It is also one of the world's top ten centres of commerce in terms of global financial flow,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> generating 6.16% of India's GDP<sup id="cite_ref-mmrda_muip_gdp_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mmrda_muip_gdp-23">[23]</a></sup> and accounting for 25% of industrial output, 70% of maritime trade in India (<a href="/wiki/Mumbai_Port_Trust" title="Mumbai Port Trust">Mumbai Port Trust</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru_Port" title="Jawaharlal Nehru Port">JNPT</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> and 70% of capital transactions to <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_India" title="Economy of India">India's economy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NMIAtender_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NMIAtender-25">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> The city houses important financial institutions such as the <a href="/wiki/Reserve_Bank_of_India" title="Reserve Bank of India">Reserve Bank of India</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bombay_Stock_Exchange" title="Bombay Stock Exchange">Bombay Stock Exchange</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Stock_Exchange_of_India" title="National Stock Exchange of India">National Stock Exchange of India</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Securities_and_Exchange_Board_of_India" title="Securities and Exchange Board of India">SEBI</a> and the corporate <a href="/wiki/List_of_Indian_companies_headquartered_in_Mumbai" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Indian companies headquartered in Mumbai">headquarters</a> of numerous <a href="/wiki/List_of_Indian_companies" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Indian companies">Indian companies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporations" class="mw-redirect" title="Multinational corporations">multinational corporations</a>. It is also home to some of India's premier scientific and nuclear institutes like <a href="/wiki/Bhabha_Atomic_Research_Centre" title="Bhabha Atomic Research Centre">BARC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_Power_Corporation_of_India" title="Nuclear Power Corporation of India">NPCL</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indian_Rare_Earths_Limited" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian Rare Earths Limited">IREL</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tata_Institute_of_Fundamental_Research" title="Tata Institute of Fundamental Research">TIFR</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atomic_Energy_Regulatory_Board" title="Atomic Energy Regulatory Board">AERB</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atomic_Energy_Commission_of_India" title="Atomic Energy Commission of India">AECI</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Atomic_Energy_(India)" class="mw-redirect" title="Department of Atomic Energy (India)">Department of Atomic Energy</a>. The city also houses India's Hindi (<a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Marathi_cinema" title="Marathi cinema">Marathi film and television</a> industry. Mumbai's business opportunities, as well as its potential to offer a higher <a href="/wiki/Standard_of_living_in_India" title="Standard of living in India">standard of living</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Corporation2007_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Corporation2007-27">[27]</a></sup> attract migrants from all over India, making the city a <a href="/wiki/Melting_pot" title="Melting pot">melting pot</a> of many communities and <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_India" title="Culture of India">cultures</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>
<p>The name <i>Mumbai</i> is derived from <i>Mumbā</i> or <i>Mahā-Ambā</i>—the name of the patron goddess (<a href="/wiki/Kuladevata" title="Kuladevata">Kuladevi</a>) <a href="/wiki/Mumbadevi" class="mw-redirect" title="Mumbadevi">Mumbadevi</a> of the native <a href="/wiki/Agri_caste" title="Agri caste">Agri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Koli_people" title="Koli people">Koli</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lunar_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Lunar Dynasty">Somvanshi Kshatriya</a> communities—<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> and <i>ā'ī</i> meaning "mother" in the <a href="/wiki/Marathi_language" title="Marathi language">Marathi</a> language, which is the mother tongue of the <a href="/wiki/Koli_people" title="Koli people">kolis</a> and the official language of Maharashtra.<sup id="cite_ref-nirc.nanzan-u.ac.jp_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nirc.nanzan-u.ac.jp-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mumbadevi_temple.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Mumbadevi_temple.jpg/170px-Mumbadevi_temple.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Mumbadevi_temple.jpg/255px-Mumbadevi_temple.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Mumbadevi_temple.jpg/340px-Mumbadevi_temple.jpg 2x" data-file-width="533" data-file-height="800" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mumbadevi_temple.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The temple of local Hindu goddess <a href="/wiki/Mumbadevi" class="mw-redirect" title="Mumbadevi">Mumbadevi</a>, from whom the city of Mumbai derives its name</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The oldest known names for the city are <i>Kakamuchee</i> and <i>Galajunkja</i>; these are sometimes still used.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Ali Muhammad Khan, in the <i>Mirat-i-Ahmedi</i> (1507) referred to the city as <i>Manbai</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> In 1508, <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portuguese</a> writer <a href="/wiki/Gaspar_Correia" title="Gaspar Correia">Gaspar Correia</a> used the name <i>Bombaim</i>, in his <i>Lendas da Índia</i> ("Legends of India").<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-et6yh_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-et6yh-34">[34]</a></sup> This name possibly originated as the <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese" title="Galician-Portuguese">Old Portuguese</a> phrase <i>bom baim</i>, meaning "good little bay",<sup id="cite_ref-Shirodkar_1998_7_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shirodkar_1998_7-35">[35]</a></sup> and <i>Bombaim</i> is still commonly used in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ety_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ety-36">[36]</a></sup> In 1516, Portuguese explorer <a href="/wiki/Duarte_Barbosa" title="Duarte Barbosa">Duarte Barbosa</a> used the name <i>Tana-Maiambu</i>: <i>Tana</i> appears to refer to the adjoining town of <a href="/wiki/Thane" title="Thane">Thane</a> and <i>Maiambu</i> to <i>Mumbadevi</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other variations recorded in the 16th and the 17th centuries include: <i>Mombayn</i> (1525), <i>Bombay</i> (1538), <i>Bombain</i> (1552), <i>Bombaym</i> (1552), <i>Monbaym</i> (1554), <i>Mombaim</i> (1563), <i>Mombaym</i> (1644), <i>Bambaye</i> (1666), <i>Bombaiim</i> (1666), <i>Bombeye</i> (1676), <i>Boon Bay</i> (1690),<sup id="cite_ref-ety_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ety-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-etyh_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etyh-38">[38]</a></sup> and <i>Bon Bahia</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/English_overseas_possessions" title="English overseas possessions">English</a> gained possession of the city in the 17th century, the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> name was <a href="/wiki/Anglicise" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglicise">anglicised</a> as <i>Bombay</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>By the late 20th century, the city was referred to as <i>Mumbai</i> or <i>Mambai</i> in the Indian statewise official languages of <a href="/wiki/Marathi_language" title="Marathi language">Marathi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Konkani_language" title="Konkani language">Konkani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gujarati_language" title="Gujarati language">Gujarati</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kannada_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Kannada language">Kannada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sindhi_language" title="Sindhi language">Sindhi</a>, and as <i>Bambai</i> in <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> The Government of India officially changed the English name to <i>Mumbai</i> in November 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> This came at the insistence of the Marathi nationalist <a href="/wiki/Shiv_Sena" title="Shiv Sena">Shiv Sena</a> party, which had just won the Maharashtra state elections, and mirrored <a href="/wiki/Renaming_of_cities_in_India" title="Renaming of cities in India">similar name changes across the country</a> and particularly in Maharashtra.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> According to <i><a href="/wiki/Slate_(magazine)" title="Slate (magazine)">Slate</a></i> magazine, "they argued that 'Bombay' was a corrupted English version of 'Mumbai' and an unwanted legacy of British colonial rule."<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> <i>Slate</i> also said "The push to rename Bombay was part of a larger movement to strengthen Marathi identity in the Maharashtra region."<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> While the city is still referred to as Bombay by some of its residents and by Indians from other regions,<sup id="cite_ref-24change_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24change-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mummaharashtra1_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mummaharashtra1-47">[47]</a></sup> mention of the city by a name other than <i>Mumbai</i> has been controversial, resulting in emotional outbursts sometimes of a violently political nature.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>A resident of Mumbai is called <i>mumbaikar</i> in the <a href="/wiki/Marathi_language" title="Marathi language">Marathi language</a>, in which the suffix <i>kar</i> means <i>resident of</i>. The term has been in use for quite some time but it gained popularity after the official name change to Mumbai.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Mumbai" title="History of Mumbai">History of Mumbai</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Mumbai_history" class="mw-redirect" title="Timeline of Mumbai history">Timeline of Mumbai history</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mumbai_03-2016_94_Kanheri_Caves.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A white Buddhist stupa." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Mumbai_03-2016_94_Kanheri_Caves.jpg/170px-Mumbai_03-2016_94_Kanheri_Caves.jpg" width="170" height="272" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Mumbai_03-2016_94_Kanheri_Caves.jpg/255px-Mumbai_03-2016_94_Kanheri_Caves.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Mumbai_03-2016_94_Kanheri_Caves.jpg/340px-Mumbai_03-2016_94_Kanheri_Caves.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2532" data-file-height="4051" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mumbai_03-2016_94_Kanheri_Caves.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Kanheri_Caves" title="Kanheri Caves">Kanheri Caves</a> served as a centre of Buddhism in Western India during ancient times</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Mumbai is built on what was once an archipelago of <a href="/wiki/Seven_islands_of_Bombay" class="mw-redirect" title="Seven islands of Bombay">seven islands</a>: <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Bombay" title="Isle of Bombay">Bombay Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parel" title="Parel">Parel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mazagaon" title="Mazagaon">Mazagaon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mahim" title="Mahim">Mahim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colaba" title="Colaba">Colaba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Worli" title="Worli">Worli</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Old_Woman%27s_Island" title="Old Woman's Island">Old Woman's Island</a> (also known as <i>Little Colaba</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> It is not exactly known when these islands were first inhabited. <a href="/wiki/Pleistocene" title="Pleistocene">Pleistocene</a> sediments found along the coastal areas around <a href="/wiki/Kandivali" title="Kandivali">Kandivali</a> in northern Mumbai suggest that the islands were inhabited since the <a href="/wiki/South_Asian_Stone_Age" title="South Asian Stone Age">Stone Age</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Perhaps at the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Common_era" class="mw-redirect" title="Common era">Common era</a> (2,000 years ago), or possibly earlier, they came to be occupied by the <a href="/wiki/Kolis" class="mw-redirect" title="Kolis">Koli</a> fishing community.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-city-profile_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-city-profile-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the third century BCE, the islands formed part of the <a href="/wiki/Maurya" class="mw-redirect" title="Maurya">Maurya</a> Empire, during its expansion in the south, ruled by the Buddhist emperor, <a href="/wiki/Ashoka" title="Ashoka">Ashoka</a> of <a href="/wiki/Magadha" title="Magadha">Magadha</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Kanheri_Caves" title="Kanheri Caves">Kanheri Caves</a> in <a href="/wiki/Borivali" title="Borivali">Borivali</a> were excavated in the mid-third century BCE,<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> and served as an important centre of Buddhism in Western India during ancient Times.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> The city then was known as <i>Heptanesia</i> (<a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">Ancient Greek</a>: A Cluster of Seven Islands) to the Greek geographer <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy" title="Ptolemy">Ptolemy</a> in 150&#160;CE.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Mahakali_Caves" title="Mahakali Caves">Mahakali Caves</a> in <a href="/wiki/Andheri" title="Andheri">Andheri</a> were built between the 1st century BCE and the 6th century CE.<sup id="cite_ref-battleneglect_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-battleneglect-59">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-threattocaves_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-threattocaves-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>Between the second century BCE and ninth century CE, the islands came under the control of successive <a href="/wiki/History_of_Mumbai_under_indigenous_empires" title="History of Mumbai under indigenous empires">indigenous dynasties</a>: <a href="/wiki/Satavahanas" class="mw-redirect" title="Satavahanas">Satavahanas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Western_Kshatrapas" class="mw-redirect" title="Western Kshatrapas">Western Kshatrapas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abhiras" class="mw-redirect" title="Abhiras">Abhiras</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vakatakas" class="mw-redirect" title="Vakatakas">Vakatakas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kalachuri" class="mw-redirect" title="Kalachuri">Kalachuris</a>, Konkan Mauryas, <a href="/wiki/Chalukya_dynasty" title="Chalukya dynasty">Chalukyas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rashtrakuta_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Rashtrakuta Dynasty">Rashtrakutas</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> before being ruled by the <a href="/wiki/Silhara_dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Silhara dynasty">Silhara dynasty</a> from 810 to 1260.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Some of the oldest edifices in the city built during this period are, <a href="/wiki/Jogeshwari_Caves" title="Jogeshwari Caves">Jogeshwari Caves</a> (between 520 and 525),<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Elephanta_Caves" title="Elephanta Caves">Elephanta Caves</a> (between the sixth to seventh century),<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Walkeshwar_Temple" title="Walkeshwar Temple">Walkeshwar Temple</a> (10th century),<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Walkeshwar_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walkeshwar-66">[66]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Banganga_Tank" title="Banganga Tank">Banganga Tank</a> (12th century).<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Banganga_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Banganga-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mumbai_03-2016_11_Haji_Ali_Dargah.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Mumbai_03-2016_11_Haji_Ali_Dargah.jpg/220px-Mumbai_03-2016_11_Haji_Ali_Dargah.jpg" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Mumbai_03-2016_11_Haji_Ali_Dargah.jpg/330px-Mumbai_03-2016_11_Haji_Ali_Dargah.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Mumbai_03-2016_11_Haji_Ali_Dargah.jpg/440px-Mumbai_03-2016_11_Haji_Ali_Dargah.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4858" data-file-height="3037" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mumbai_03-2016_11_Haji_Ali_Dargah.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Haji_Ali_Dargah" title="Haji Ali Dargah">Haji Ali Dargah</a> was built in 1431, when Mumbai was under the rule of the <a href="/wiki/Gujarat_Sultanate" title="Gujarat Sultanate">Gujarat Sultanate</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bhima_of_Mahikavati" title="Bhima of Mahikavati">King Bhimdev</a> founded his kingdom in the region in the late 13th century and established his capital in <i>Mahikawati</i> (present day <a href="/wiki/Mahim" title="Mahim">Mahim</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Pathare_Prabhu" title="Pathare Prabhu">Pathare Prabhus</a>, among the earliest known settlers of the city, were brought to <i>Mahikawati</i> from <a href="/wiki/Saurashtra_(region)" title="Saurashtra (region)">Saurashtra</a> in Gujarat around 1298 by Bhimdev.<sup id="cite_ref-prabhu_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prabhu-70">[70]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Sultanate" title="Delhi Sultanate">Delhi Sultanate</a> annexed the islands in 1347–48 and controlled it until 1407. During this time, the islands were administered by the Muslim Governors of <a href="/wiki/Gujarat" title="Gujarat">Gujarat</a>, who were appointed by the Delhi Sultanate.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>The islands were later governed by the independent <a href="/wiki/Gujarat_Sultanate" title="Gujarat Sultanate">Gujarat Sultanate</a>, which was established in 1407. The Sultanate's patronage led to the construction of many mosques, prominent being the <a href="/wiki/Haji_Ali_Dargah" title="Haji Ali Dargah">Haji Ali Dargah</a> in <a href="/wiki/Worli" title="Worli">Worli</a>, built in honour of the Muslim saint Haji Ali in 1431.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> From 1429 to 1431, the islands were a source of contention between the Gujarat Sultanate and the <a href="/wiki/Bahamani_Sultanate" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahamani Sultanate">Bahamani Sultanate</a> of Deccan.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mis_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mis-75">[75]</a></sup> In 1493, <a href="/wiki/Bahadur_Khan_Gilani" title="Bahadur Khan Gilani">Bahadur Khan Gilani</a> of the Bahamani Sultanate attempted to conquer the islands but was defeated.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Portuguese_and_British_rule">Portuguese and British rule</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Bombay_under_Portuguese_rule_(1534%E2%80%931661)" title="History of Bombay under Portuguese rule (1534–1661)">History of Bombay under Portuguese rule (1534–1661)</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Bombay_under_British_rule" title="History of Bombay under British rule">History of Bombay under British rule</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Madh-fort3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Madh-fort3.jpg/220px-Madh-fort3.jpg" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Madh-fort3.jpg/330px-Madh-fort3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Madh-fort3.jpg/440px-Madh-fort3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="452" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Madh-fort3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Madh_Fort" title="Madh Fort">Madh Fort</a> built by the Portuguese, was one of the most important forts in <a href="/wiki/Salsette" class="mw-redirect" title="Salsette">Salsette</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughal Empire</a>, founded in 1526, was the dominant power in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a> during the mid-16th century.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Growing apprehensive of the power of the <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughal</a> emperor <a href="/wiki/Humayun" title="Humayun">Humayun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bahadur_Shah_of_Gujarat" title="Bahadur Shah of Gujarat">Sultan Bahadur Shah</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Gujarat_Sultanate" title="Gujarat Sultanate">Gujarat Sultanate</a> was obliged to sign the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Bassein_(1534)" title="Treaty of Bassein (1534)">Treaty of Bassein</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a> on 23 December 1534. According to the treaty, the seven islands of Bombay, the nearby strategic town of <a href="/wiki/Vasai" title="Vasai">Bassein</a> and its dependencies were offered to the Portuguese. The territories were later surrendered on 25 October 1535.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Portuguese were actively involved in the foundation and growth of their Roman Catholic religious orders in Bombay.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> They called the islands by various names, which finally took the written form <i>Bombaim</i>. The islands were leased to several Portuguese officers during their regime. The Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Franciscans" title="Franciscans">Franciscans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jesuits" class="mw-redirect" title="Jesuits">Jesuits</a> built several churches in the city, prominent being the <a href="/wiki/St._Michael%27s_Church_(Mumbai)" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Michael's Church (Mumbai)">St. Michael's Church</a> at <a href="/wiki/Mahim" title="Mahim">Mahim</a> (1534),<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/St._John_the_Baptist_Church,_Mumbai" title="St. John the Baptist Church, Mumbai">St. John the Baptist Church</a> at <a href="/wiki/Andheri" title="Andheri">Andheri</a> (1579),<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/St._Andrew%27s_Church_(Mumbai)" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Andrew's Church (Mumbai)">St. Andrew's Church</a> at <a href="/wiki/Bandra" title="Bandra">Bandra</a> (1580),<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Gloria_Church" title="Gloria Church">Gloria Church</a> at <a href="/wiki/Byculla" title="Byculla">Byculla</a> (1632).<sup id="cite_ref-gc_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gc-83">[83]</a></sup> The Portuguese also built several fortifications around the city like the <a href="/wiki/Bombay_Castle" title="Bombay Castle">Bombay Castle</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Castella_de_Aguada" title="Castella de Aguada">Castella de Aguada</a></i> (Castelo da Aguada or Bandra Fort), and <a href="/wiki/Madh_Fort" title="Madh Fort">Madh Fort</a>. The <a href="/wiki/English_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="English Empire">English</a> were in constant struggle with the Portuguese vying for hegemony over Bombay, as they recognised its strategic natural harbour and its natural isolation from land-attacks. By the middle of the 17th century the growing power of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">Dutch Empire</a> forced the <a href="/wiki/English_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="English Empire">English</a> to acquire a station in western India. On 11 May 1661, the marriage treaty of <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">Charles II of England</a> and <a href="/wiki/Catherine_of_Braganza" title="Catherine of Braganza">Catherine of Braganza</a>, daughter of <a href="/wiki/John_IV_of_Portugal" title="John IV of Portugal">King John IV of Portugal</a>, placed the islands in possession of the <a href="/wiki/English_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="English Empire">English Empire</a>, as part of Catherine's dowry to Charles.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> However, <a href="/wiki/Salsette_Island" title="Salsette Island">Salsette</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vasai" title="Vasai">Bassein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mazagaon" title="Mazagaon">Mazagaon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parel" title="Parel">Parel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Worli" title="Worli">Worli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sion,_Mumbai" title="Sion, Mumbai">Sion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dharavi" title="Dharavi">Dharavi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wadala_Road" class="mw-redirect" title="Wadala Road">Wadala</a> still remained under Portuguese possession. From 1665 to 1666, the English managed to acquire Mahim, Sion, Dharavi, and Wadala.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AMH-6748-NA_Two_views_of_the_English_fort_in_Bombay.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/AMH-6748-NA_Two_views_of_the_English_fort_in_Bombay.jpg/220px-AMH-6748-NA_Two_views_of_the_English_fort_in_Bombay.jpg" width="220" height="197" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/AMH-6748-NA_Two_views_of_the_English_fort_in_Bombay.jpg/330px-AMH-6748-NA_Two_views_of_the_English_fort_in_Bombay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/AMH-6748-NA_Two_views_of_the_English_fort_in_Bombay.jpg/440px-AMH-6748-NA_Two_views_of_the_English_fort_in_Bombay.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="2145" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AMH-6748-NA_Two_views_of_the_English_fort_in_Bombay.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Two views of the English fort in Bombay, c. 1665</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In accordance with the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Charter_of_27_March_1668" title="Royal Charter of 27 March 1668">Royal Charter of 27 March 1668</a>, England leased these islands to the <a href="/wiki/English_East_India_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="English East India Company">English East India Company</a> in 1668 for a sum of <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">£</a>10 per annum.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> The population quickly rose from 10,000 in 1661, to 60,000 in 1675.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> The islands were subsequently attacked by <a href="/wiki/Yakut_Khan" title="Yakut Khan">Yakut Khan</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Siddi" title="Siddi">Siddi</a> admiral of the <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughal Empire</a>, in October 1672,<sup id="cite_ref-y72_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-y72-88">[88]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rickloffe_van_Goen" class="mw-redirect" title="Rickloffe van Goen">Rickloffe van Goen</a>, the Governor-General of <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">Dutch India</a> on 20 February 1673,<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Siddi" title="Siddi">Siddi</a> admiral <a href="/wiki/Siddi_Sambal" title="Siddi Sambal">Sambal</a> on 10 October 1673.<sup id="cite_ref-y72_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-y72-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1687, the English East India Company transferred its headquarters from <a href="/wiki/Surat" title="Surat">Surat</a> to Bombay. The city eventually became the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Bombay_Presidency" title="Bombay Presidency">Bombay Presidency</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> Following the transfer, Bombay was placed at the head of all the company's establishments in India.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> Towards the end of the 17th century, the islands again suffered incursions from Yakut Khan in 1689–90.<sup id="cite_ref-iexpress_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iexpress-92">[92]</a></sup> The Portuguese presence ended in Bombay when the <a href="/wiki/Maratha_Empire" title="Maratha Empire">Marathas</a> under <i><a href="/wiki/Peshwa" title="Peshwa">Peshwa</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Baji_Rao_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Baji Rao I">Baji Rao I</a> captured <a href="/wiki/Salsette_Island" title="Salsette Island">Salsette</a> in 1737, and <a href="/wiki/Vasai" title="Vasai">Bassein</a> in 1739.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> By the middle of the 18th century, Bombay began to grow into a major trading town, and received a huge influx of migrants from across India.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Later, the British occupied Salsette on 28 December 1774. With the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Surat" title="Treaty of Surat">Treaty of Surat</a> (1775), the British formally gained control of <a href="/wiki/Salsette" class="mw-redirect" title="Salsette">Salsette</a> and Bassein, resulting in the <a href="/wiki/First_Anglo-Maratha_War" title="First Anglo-Maratha War">First Anglo-Maratha War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> The British were able to secure Salsette from the Marathas without violence through the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Purandar_(1776)" title="Treaty of Purandar (1776)">Treaty of Purandar</a> (1776),<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> and later through the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Salbai" title="Treaty of Salbai">Treaty of Salbai</a> (1782), signed to settle the outcome of the First Anglo-Maratha War.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ships_in_Bombay_Harbour,_1731.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Ships_in_Bombay_Harbour%2C_1731.jpg/220px-Ships_in_Bombay_Harbour%2C_1731.jpg" width="220" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Ships_in_Bombay_Harbour%2C_1731.jpg/330px-Ships_in_Bombay_Harbour%2C_1731.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Ships_in_Bombay_Harbour%2C_1731.jpg/440px-Ships_in_Bombay_Harbour%2C_1731.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="610" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ships_in_Bombay_Harbour,_1731.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ships in <a href="/wiki/Bombay_Harbour" class="mw-redirect" title="Bombay Harbour">Bombay Harbour</a> (c. 1731). Bombay emerged as a significant trading town during the mid-18th century.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>From 1782 onwards, the city was reshaped with large-scale civil engineering projects aimed at merging all the seven islands into a single amalgamated mass. This project, known as <a href="/wiki/Hornby_Vellard" title="Hornby Vellard">Hornby Vellard</a>, was completed by 1784.<sup id="cite_ref-Dwivedi_2001_28_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dwivedi_2001_28-18">[18]</a></sup> In 1817, the British East India Company under <a href="/wiki/Mountstuart_Elphinstone" title="Mountstuart Elphinstone">Mountstuart Elphinstone</a> defeated <a href="/wiki/Baji_Rao_II" title="Baji Rao II">Baji Rao II</a>, the last of the Maratha <i>Peshwa</i> in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Khadki" title="Battle of Khadki">Battle of Khadki</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> Following his defeat, almost the whole of the Deccan came under British suzerainty, and was incorporated into the Bombay Presidency. The success of the British campaign in the Deccan marked the end of all attacks by native powers.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>By 1845, the seven islands coalesced into a single landmass by the Hornby Vellard project via large scale <a href="/wiki/Land_reclamation" title="Land reclamation">land reclamation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-fp-onceuponatime_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fp-onceuponatime-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mumfact_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mumfact-100">[100]</a></sup> On 16 April 1853, India's first passenger railway line was established, connecting Bombay to the neighbouring town of <a href="/wiki/Thane" title="Thane">Thana</a> (now Thane).<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a> (1861–1865), the city became the world's chief cotton-trading market, resulting in a boom in the economy that subsequently enhanced the city's stature.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>The opening of the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a> in 1869 transformed Bombay into one of the largest seaports on the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Sea" title="Arabian Sea">Arabian Sea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> In September 1896, Bombay was hit by a <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_plague_epidemic" class="mw-redirect" title="Mumbai plague epidemic">bubonic plague epidemic</a> where the death toll was estimated at 1,900 people per week.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> About 850,000 people fled Bombay and the textile industry was adversely affected.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> As the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Bombay_Presidency" title="Bombay Presidency">Bombay Presidency</a>, the city witnessed the <a href="/wiki/Indian_independence_movement" title="Indian independence movement">Indian independence movement</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Quit_India_Movement" title="Quit India Movement">Quit India Movement</a> in 1942 and <a href="/wiki/The_Royal_Indian_Navy_Mutiny" class="mw-redirect" title="The Royal Indian Navy Mutiny">The Royal Indian Navy Mutiny</a> in 1946 being its most notable events.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independent_India">Independent India</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Bombay_in_Independent_India" class="mw-redirect" title="History of Bombay in Independent India">History of Bombay in Independent India</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Victoria_Terminus,_Bombay_in_1950.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Victoria_Terminus%2C_Bombay_in_1950.jpg/220px-Victoria_Terminus%2C_Bombay_in_1950.jpg" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Victoria_Terminus%2C_Bombay_in_1950.jpg/330px-Victoria_Terminus%2C_Bombay_in_1950.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Victoria_Terminus%2C_Bombay_in_1950.jpg/440px-Victoria_Terminus%2C_Bombay_in_1950.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="638" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Victoria_Terminus,_Bombay_in_1950.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Victoria Terminus, Bombay in 1950</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After India's independence in 1947, the territory of the <a href="/wiki/Bombay_Presidency" title="Bombay Presidency">Bombay Presidency</a> retained by India was restructured into <a href="/wiki/Bombay_State" title="Bombay State">Bombay State</a>. The area of Bombay State increased, after several erstwhile princely states that joined the Indian union were integrated into the state. Subsequently, the city became the capital of Bombay State.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> On April 1950, Municipal limits of Bombay were expanded by merging the <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_suburban_district" class="mw-redirect" title="Mumbai suburban district">Bombay Suburban District</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_city_district" class="mw-redirect" title="Mumbai city district">Bombay City</a> to form the Greater Bombay Municipal Corporation.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Samyukta_Maharashtra_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Samyukta Maharashtra movement">Samyukta Maharashtra movement</a> to create a separate Maharashtra state including Bombay was at its height in the 1950s. In the <i><a href="/wiki/Lok_Sabha" title="Lok Sabha">Lok Sabha</a></i> discussions in 1955, the <a href="/wiki/Indian_National_Congress" title="Indian National Congress">Congress party</a> demanded that the city be constituted as an autonomous city-state.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/States_Reorganisation_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="States Reorganisation Act">States Reorganisation</a> Committee recommended a bilingual state for Maharashtra–<a href="/wiki/Gujarat" title="Gujarat">Gujarat</a> with Bombay as its capital in its 1955 report. <a href="/wiki/Bombay_Citizens%27_Committee" title="Bombay Citizens' Committee">Bombay Citizens' Committee</a>, an advocacy group of leading <a href="/wiki/Gujarati_people" title="Gujarati people">Gujarati</a> industrialists lobbied for Bombay's independent status.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following protests during the movement in which 105 people lost their lives in clashes with the police, Bombay State was reorganised on linguistic lines on 1 May 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gujarati_language" title="Gujarati language">Gujarati</a>-speaking areas of Bombay State were partitioned into the state of Gujarat.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Maharashtra State with Bombay as its capital was formed with the merger of <a href="/wiki/Marathi_language" title="Marathi language">Marathi</a>-speaking areas of Bombay State, eight districts from <a href="/wiki/Central_Provinces_and_Berar" title="Central Provinces and Berar">Central Provinces and Berar</a>, five districts from <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad_State" title="Hyderabad State">Hyderabad State</a>, and numerous princely states enclosed between them.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> As a memorial to the martyrs of the Samyukta Maharashtra movement, Flora Fountain was renamed as <i><a href="/wiki/Hutatma_Chowk" title="Hutatma Chowk">Hutatma Chowk</a></i> (Martyr's Square), and a memorial was erected.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hutatma_Chowk.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A stone statue of torch-bearers as seen at night. A fountain with a white base is in the background" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Hutatma_Chowk.jpg/170px-Hutatma_Chowk.jpg" width="170" height="288" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Hutatma_Chowk.jpg/255px-Hutatma_Chowk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Hutatma_Chowk.jpg/340px-Hutatma_Chowk.jpg 2x" data-file-width="451" data-file-height="763" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hutatma_Chowk.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Hutatma_Chowk" title="Hutatma Chowk">Hutatma Chowk</a> memorial, built to honour the martyrs of the <a href="/wiki/Samyukta_Maharashtra_Samiti" class="mw-redirect" title="Samyukta Maharashtra Samiti">Samyukta Maharashtra movement</a> (<a href="/wiki/Flora_Fountain" title="Flora Fountain">Flora Fountain</a> is on its left in the background.)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The following decades saw massive expansion of the city and its suburbs. In the late 1960s, <a href="/wiki/Nariman_Point" title="Nariman Point">Nariman Point</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cuffe_Parade" title="Cuffe Parade">Cuffe Parade</a> were reclaimed and developed.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_Metropolitan_Region_Development_Authority" title="Mumbai Metropolitan Region Development Authority">Bombay Metropolitan Region Development Authority</a> (BMRDA) was established on 26 January 1975 by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Maharashtra" title="Government of Maharashtra">Government of Maharashtra</a> as an apex body for planning and co-ordination of development activities in the <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_metropolitan_area" class="mw-redirect" title="Mumbai metropolitan area">Bombay metropolitan region</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> In August 1979, a sister township of <a href="/wiki/New_Bombay" class="mw-redirect" title="New Bombay">New Bombay</a> was founded by the <a href="/wiki/City_and_Industrial_Development_Corporation" title="City and Industrial Development Corporation">City and Industrial Development Corporation</a> (CIDCO) across the <a href="/wiki/Thane_district" title="Thane district">Thane</a> and <a href="/wiki/Raigad_district" title="Raigad district">Raigad districts</a> to help the dispersal and control of Bombay's population. The textile industry in Bombay largely disappeared after the widespread 1982 <a href="/wiki/Great_Bombay_Textile_Strike" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Bombay Textile Strike">Great Bombay Textile Strike</a>, in which nearly 250,000 workers in more than 50 textile mills went on strike.<sup id="cite_ref-a_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-a-118">[118]</a></sup> Mumbai's defunct cotton mills have since become the focus of <a href="/wiki/Redevelopment_of_Mumbai_mills" title="Redevelopment of Mumbai mills">intense redevelopment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-skylimit_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-skylimit-119">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-revisitmills_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-revisitmills-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru_Port" title="Jawaharlal Nehru Port">Jawaharlal Nehru Port</a>, which currently handles 55–60% of India's containerised cargo, was commissioned on 26 May 1989 across the creek at <a href="/wiki/Nhava_Sheva" class="mw-redirect" title="Nhava Sheva">Nhava Sheva</a> with a view to de-congest <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_Harbour" title="Mumbai Harbour">Bombay Harbour</a> and to serve as a hub port for the city.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> The geographical limits of Greater Bombay were coextensive with municipal limits of Greater Bombay. On 1 October 1990, the Greater Bombay district was bifurcated to form two revenue districts namely, <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_City_district" title="Mumbai City district">Bombay City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_Suburban_district" title="Mumbai Suburban district">Bombay Suburban</a>, though they continued to be administered by same Municipal Administration.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<p>From 1990 to 2010, there has been an increase in violence in the hitherto largely peaceful city. Following the demolition of the <a href="/wiki/Babri_Masjid" title="Babri Masjid">Babri Masjid</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ayodhya" title="Ayodhya">Ayodhya</a>, the city was rocked by the <a href="/wiki/Bombay_Riots" class="mw-redirect" title="Bombay Riots">Hindu-Muslim riots of 1992–93</a> in which more than 1,000&#160;people were killed. On 12 March 1993, <a href="/wiki/1993_Bombay_bombings" title="1993 Bombay bombings">a series of 13 co-ordinated bombings</a> at several city landmarks by Islamic extremists and the <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_underworld#Mumbai_underworld" class="mw-redirect" title="Mumbai underworld">Bombay underworld</a> resulted in 257 deaths and over 700 injuries.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> In 2006, 209 people were killed and over 700 injured when <a href="/wiki/11_July_2006_Mumbai_train_bombings" class="mw-redirect" title="11 July 2006 Mumbai train bombings">seven bombs exploded</a> on the city's <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_Suburban_Railway" title="Mumbai Suburban Railway">commuter trains</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> In 2008, a series of <a href="/wiki/26_November_2008_Mumbai_attacks" class="mw-redirect" title="26 November 2008 Mumbai attacks">ten coordinated attacks</a> by armed terrorists for three days resulted in 173 deaths, 308 injuries, and severe damage to several heritage landmarks and prestigious hotels.<sup id="cite_ref-Casualties_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Casualties-125">[125]</a></sup> The blasts that occurred at the Opera House, Zaveri Bazaar, and Dadar on <a href="/wiki/13_July_2011_Mumbai_bombings" class="mw-redirect" title="13 July 2011 Mumbai bombings">13 July 2011</a> were the latest in the series of terrorist attacks in Mumbai.<sup id="cite_ref-13_July_Mumbai_bombings_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13_July_Mumbai_bombings-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mumbai is the commercial capital of India and has evolved into a global financial hub.<sup id="cite_ref-Mumbai_global_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mumbai_global-127">[127]</a></sup> For several decades it has been the home of India's main financial services, and a focus for both infrastructure development and private investment.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> From being an ancient fishing community and a colonial centre of trade, Mumbai has become South Asia's largest city and home of the world's most prolific film industry.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Mumbai" title="Geography of Mumbai">Geography of Mumbai</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/South_Mumbai" title="South Mumbai">South Mumbai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Western_Suburbs_(Mumbai)" title="Western Suburbs (Mumbai)">Western Suburbs (Mumbai)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Suburbs_(Mumbai)" title="Eastern Suburbs (Mumbai)">Eastern Suburbs (Mumbai)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_neighbourhoods_in_Mumbai" title="List of neighbourhoods in Mumbai">List of neighbourhoods in Mumbai</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mumbaicitydistricts.png" class="image"><img alt="Mumbai is on a narrow peninsula on the southwest of Salsette Island, which lies between the Arabian Sea to the west, Thane Creek to the east, and Vasai Creek to the north. Mumbai's suburban district occupies most of the island. Navi Mumbai is east of Thane Creek, and the Thane District is north of Vasai Creek." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Mumbaicitydistricts.png/170px-Mumbaicitydistricts.png" width="170" height="288" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/57/Mumbaicitydistricts.png 1.5x" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="339" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mumbaicitydistricts.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mumbai consists of two revenue districts</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Mumbai consists of two distinct regions: <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_City_district" title="Mumbai City district">Mumbai City district</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_Suburban_district" title="Mumbai Suburban district">Mumbai Suburban district</a>, which form two separate revenue districts of Maharashtra.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> The city district region is also commonly referred to as the <i>Island City</i> or <a href="/wiki/South_Mumbai" title="South Mumbai">South Mumbai</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mmrda_muip_gdp_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mmrda_muip_gdp-23">[23]</a></sup> The total area of Mumbai is 603.4&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (233 sq mi).<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> Of this, the island city spans 67.79&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (26 sq mi), while the suburban district spans 370&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (143 sq mi), together accounting for 437.71&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (169 sq mi) under the administration of <a href="/wiki/Municipal_Corporation_of_Greater_Mumbai" class="mw-redirect" title="Municipal Corporation of Greater Mumbai">Municipal Corporation of Greater Mumbai</a> (MCGM). The remaining areas belong to various Defence establishments, the <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_Port_Trust" title="Mumbai Port Trust">Mumbai Port Trust</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Atomic_Energy_Commission_of_India" title="Atomic Energy Commission of India">Atomic Energy Commission</a> and the Borivali National Park, which are out of the jurisdiction of the MCGM.<sup id="cite_ref-trf_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trf-132">[132]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_Metropolitan_Region" title="Mumbai Metropolitan Region">Mumbai Metropolitan Region</a> which includes portions of <a href="/wiki/Thane_district" title="Thane district">Thane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palghar_district" title="Palghar district">Palghar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Raigad_district" title="Raigad district">Raigad</a> districts in addition to Greater Mumbai, covers an area of 4,355&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (1681.5 sq mi).<sup id="cite_ref-projectsecoa1_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-projectsecoa1-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mumbai lies at the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Ulhas_River" title="Ulhas River">Ulhas River</a> on the western coast of India, in the coastal region known as the <a href="/wiki/Konkan" title="Konkan">Konkan</a>. It sits on <a href="/wiki/Salsette_Island" title="Salsette Island">Salsette Island</a> (Sashti Island), which it partially shares with the <a href="/wiki/Thane_district" title="Thane district">Thane district</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-geo_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geo-133">[133]</a></sup> Mumbai is bounded by the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Sea" title="Arabian Sea">Arabian Sea</a> to the west.<sup id="cite_ref-mloc_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mloc-134">[134]</a></sup> Many parts of the city lie just above sea level, with elevations ranging from 10&#160;m (33&#160;ft) to 15&#160;m (49&#160;ft);<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> the city has an average elevation of 14&#160;m (46&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-Wbase_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wbase-136">[136]</a></sup> Northern Mumbai (Salsette) is hilly,<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> and the highest point in the city is 450 m (1,476&#160;ft) at Salsette in the <a href="/wiki/Powai" title="Powai">Powai</a>–<a href="/wiki/Kanheri" class="mw-redirect" title="Kanheri">Kanheri</a> ranges.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sanjay_Gandhi_National_Park" title="Sanjay Gandhi National Park">Sanjay Gandhi National Park</a> (Borivali National Park) is located partly in the <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_suburban_district" class="mw-redirect" title="Mumbai suburban district">Mumbai suburban district</a>, and partly in the Thane district, and it extends over an area of 103.09&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (39.80 sq mi).<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>Apart from the <a href="/wiki/Bhatsa_Dam" title="Bhatsa Dam">Bhatsa Dam</a>, there are six major lakes that supply water to the city: <a href="/wiki/Vihar_Lake" title="Vihar Lake">Vihar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Middle_Vaitarna_Dam" title="Middle Vaitarna Dam">Lower Vaitarna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Upper_Vaitarna_Dam" class="mw-redirect" title="Upper Vaitarna Dam">Upper Vaitarna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tulsi_Lake" title="Tulsi Lake">Tulsi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tansa_Dam" title="Tansa Dam">Tansa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Powai" title="Powai">Powai</a>. Tulsi Lake and Vihar Lake are located in <a href="/wiki/Borivili_National_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Borivili National Park">Borivili National Park</a>, within the city's limits. The supply from Powai lake, also within the city limits, is used only for agricultural and industrial purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> Three small rivers, the <a href="/wiki/Dahisar_River" title="Dahisar River">Dahisar River</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poisar_River" title="Poisar River">Poinsar (or Poisar)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oshiwara_River" title="Oshiwara River">Ohiwara (or Oshiwara)</a> originate within the park, while the polluted <a href="/wiki/Mithi_River" title="Mithi River">Mithi River</a> originates from Tulsi Lake and gathers water overflowing from Vihar and Powai Lakes.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> The coastline of the city is indented with numerous <a href="/wiki/Creek_(tidal)" title="Creek (tidal)">creeks</a> and bays, stretching from the <a href="/wiki/Thane_creek" class="mw-redirect" title="Thane creek">Thane creek</a> on the eastern to Madh Marve on the western front.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> The eastern coast of Salsette Island is covered with large <a href="/wiki/Mangrove" title="Mangrove">mangrove</a> <a href="/wiki/Swamp" title="Swamp">swamps</a>, rich in biodiversity, while the western coast is mostly sandy and rocky.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p>
<p>Soil cover in the city region is predominantly sandy due to its proximity to the sea. In the suburbs, the soil cover is largely alluvial and loamy.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> The underlying rock of the region is composed of black <a href="/wiki/Deccan" class="mw-redirect" title="Deccan">Deccan</a> basalt flows, and their acidic and <a href="/wiki/Basic_(chemistry)" class="mw-redirect" title="Basic (chemistry)">basic</a> variants dating back to the late <a href="/wiki/Cretaceous" title="Cretaceous">Cretaceous</a> and early <a href="/wiki/Eocene" title="Eocene">Eocene</a> eras.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> Mumbai sits on a <a href="/wiki/Seismology" title="Seismology">seismically active zone</a> owing to the presence of 23 fault lines in the vicinity.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> The area is classified as a <a href="/wiki/Earthquake_hazard_zoning_of_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Earthquake hazard zoning of India">Seismic Zone III region</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> which means an earthquake of up to magnitude 6.5 on the Richter scale may be expected.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:India_mumbai_temperature_precipitation_averages_chart.svg" class="image"><img alt="The average temperature ranges between 23&#160;°C (73&#160;°F) in January to 30&#160;°C (86&#160;°F) in May. Rainfall is at or near zero from November through May, then quickly rises to a peak of about 600&#160;mm (23.62&#160;in) in July, falling back more gradually." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/India_mumbai_temperature_precipitation_averages_chart.svg/220px-India_mumbai_temperature_precipitation_averages_chart.svg.png" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/India_mumbai_temperature_precipitation_averages_chart.svg/330px-India_mumbai_temperature_precipitation_averages_chart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/India_mumbai_temperature_precipitation_averages_chart.svg/440px-India_mumbai_temperature_precipitation_averages_chart.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="562" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:India_mumbai_temperature_precipitation_averages_chart.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Average temperature and precipitation in Mumbai</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Mumbai" title="Climate of Mumbai">Climate of Mumbai</a></div>
<p>Mumbai has a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical climate</a>, specifically a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_savanna_climate" title="Tropical savanna climate">tropical wet and dry climate</a> (Aw) under the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>, with seven months of dryness and peak of rains in July.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> The cooler season from December to February is followed by the summer season from March to June. The period from June to about the end of September constitutes the south-west monsoon season, and October and November form the post-monsoon season.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></p>
<p>Between June and September, the <a href="/wiki/Monsoon_of_Indian_subcontinent" class="mw-redirect" title="Monsoon of Indian subcontinent">south west monsoon</a> rains lash the city. Pre-monsoon showers are received in May. Occasionally, north-east monsoon showers occur in October and November. The maximum annual rainfall ever recorded was 3,452&#160;mm (136&#160;in) for 1954.<sup id="cite_ref-clra_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clra-151">[151]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/2005_Mumbai_floods" class="mw-redirect" title="2005 Mumbai floods">highest rainfall</a> recorded in a single day was 944&#160;mm (37&#160;in) on <a href="/wiki/Maharashtra_floods_of_2005" title="Maharashtra floods of 2005">26 July 2005</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> The average total annual rainfall is 2,146.6&#160;mm (85&#160;in) for the Island City, and 2,457&#160;mm (97&#160;in) for the suburbs.<sup id="cite_ref-clra_151-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clra-151">[151]</a></sup></p>
<p>The average annual temperature is 27.2&#160;°C (81&#160;°F), and the average annual <a href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">precipitation</a> is 2,167&#160;mm (85&#160;in).<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> In the Island City, the average maximum temperature is 31.2&#160;°C (88&#160;°F), while the average minimum temperature is 23.7&#160;°C (75&#160;°F). In the suburbs, the daily mean maximum temperature range from 29.1&#160;°C (84&#160;°F) to 33.3&#160;°C (92&#160;°F), while the daily mean minimum temperature ranges from 16.3&#160;°C (61&#160;°F) to 26.2&#160;°C (79&#160;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-clra_151-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clra-151">[151]</a></sup> The record high is 42.2&#160;°C (108&#160;°F) set on 14 April 1952,<sup id="cite_ref-IMD2_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMD2-154">[154]</a></sup> and the record low is 7.4&#160;°C (45&#160;°F) set on 27 January 1962.<sup id="cite_ref-IMD2_154-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMD2-154">[154]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup></p>
