<p><br /></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Mumbai" title="Economy of Mumbai">Economy of Mumbai</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bombay_Stock_Exchange,_Mumbai.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Bombay_Stock_Exchange%2C_Mumbai.jpg/220px-Bombay_Stock_Exchange%2C_Mumbai.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Bombay_Stock_Exchange%2C_Mumbai.jpg/330px-Bombay_Stock_Exchange%2C_Mumbai.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Bombay_Stock_Exchange%2C_Mumbai.jpg/440px-Bombay_Stock_Exchange%2C_Mumbai.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="1024" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bombay_Stock_Exchange,_Mumbai.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Bombay_Stock_Exchange" title="Bombay Stock Exchange">Bombay Stock Exchange</a> is the oldest stock exchange in Asia.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Mumbai is India's largest city (by population) and is the financial and commercial capital of the country as it generates 6.16% of the total GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-mmrda_muip_gdp_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mmrda_muip_gdp-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Mumbai_global_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mumbai_global-127">[127]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Financial_Express_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Financial_Express-158">[158]</a></sup> It serves as an economic hub of India, contributing 10% of factory employment, 25% of industrial output, 33% of <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">income tax</a> collections, 60% of <a href="/wiki/Customs_(tax)" class="mw-redirect" title="Customs (tax)">customs duty</a> collections, 20% of central <a href="/wiki/Excise_tax" class="mw-redirect" title="Excise tax">excise tax</a> collections, 40% of India's <a href="/wiki/Foreign_trade" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign trade">foreign trade</a> and <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>4,000 crore</span> (US$590&#160;million) in <a href="/wiki/Corporate_tax" title="Corporate tax">corporate taxes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> Along with the rest of India, Mumbai has witnessed an economic boom since the liberalisation of 1991, the finance boom in the mid-nineties and the IT, export, services and outsourcing boom in 2000s.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> Although Mumbai had prominently figured as the hub of economic activity of India in the 1990s, the <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_Metropolitan_Region" title="Mumbai Metropolitan Region">Mumbai Metropolitan Region</a> is presently witnessing a reduction in its contribution to India's GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-ecoprofile_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ecoprofile-161">[161]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of October 2015, Mumbai's GDP is $278 billion (from 2014).<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> and its per-capita (PPP) income in 2009 was <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>486,000</span> (US$7,200),<sup id="cite_ref-livemint.com_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-livemint.com-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-percapita_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-percapita-164">[164]</a></sup> which is almost three times the national average.<sup id="cite_ref-mumfact_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mumfact-100">[100]</a></sup> Its nominal per capita income is <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>125,000</span> (US$1,900),<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> (US$2,094). Many of India's numerous conglomerates (including <a href="/wiki/Larsen_%26_Toubro" title="Larsen &amp; Toubro">Larsen &amp; Toubro</a>, <a href="/wiki/State_Bank_of_India" title="State Bank of India">State Bank of India</a> (SBI), <a href="/wiki/Life_Insurance_Corporation_of_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Life Insurance Corporation of India">Life Insurance Corporation of India</a> (LIC), <a href="/wiki/Tata_Group" title="Tata Group">Tata Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Godrej_Group" title="Godrej Group">Godrej</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reliance_Industries" title="Reliance Industries">Reliance</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-Mumbai_global_127-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mumbai_global-127">[127]</a></sup> and five of the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_Global_500" title="Fortune Global 500">Fortune Global 500</a> companies are based in Mumbai.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> This is facilitated by the presence of the <a href="/wiki/Reserve_Bank_of_India" title="Reserve Bank of India">Reserve Bank of India</a> (RBI), the <a href="/wiki/Bombay_Stock_Exchange" title="Bombay Stock Exchange">Bombay Stock Exchange</a> (BSE), the <a href="/wiki/National_Stock_Exchange_of_India" title="National Stock Exchange of India">National Stock Exchange of India</a> (NSE), and financial sector regulators such as the <a href="/wiki/Securities_and_Exchange_Board_of_India" title="Securities and Exchange Board of India">Securities and Exchange Board of India</a> (SEBI).<sup id="cite_ref-ecoprofile_161-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ecoprofile-161">[161]</a></sup></p>
<p>Until the 1970s, Mumbai owed its prosperity largely to textile mills and the seaport, but the local economy has since then diversified to include <a href="/wiki/Finance" title="Finance">finance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Engineering" title="Engineering">engineering</a>, diamond-polishing, <a href="/wiki/Healthcare" class="mw-redirect" title="Healthcare">healthcare</a> and information technology.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> The key sectors contributing to the city's economy are: finance, gems &amp; jewellery, leather processing, IT and <a href="/wiki/Business_process_outsourcing" title="Business process outsourcing">ITES</a>, textiles, and entertainment. <a href="/wiki/Nariman_Point" title="Nariman Point">Nariman Point</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bandra_Kurla_Complex" title="Bandra Kurla Complex">Bandra Kurla Complex</a> (BKC) are Mumbai's major financial centres.<sup id="cite_ref-ecoprofile_161-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ecoprofile-161">[161]</a></sup> Despite competition from <a href="/wiki/Bangalore" title="Bangalore">Bangalore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad" title="Hyderabad">Hyderabad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pune" title="Pune">Pune</a>, Mumbai has carved a niche for itself in the information technology industry. The <a href="/wiki/SEEPZ" title="SEEPZ">Santacruz Electronic Export Processing Zone</a> (SEEPZ) and the International Infotech Park (<a href="/wiki/Navi_Mumbai" title="Navi Mumbai">Navi Mumbai</a>) offer excellent facilities to IT companies.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup></p>
<p>State and central government employees make up a large percentage of the city's workforce. Mumbai also has a large unskilled and semi-skilled self-employed population, who primarily earn their livelihood as hawkers, taxi drivers, mechanics and other such <a href="/wiki/Blue_collar" class="mw-redirect" title="Blue collar">blue collar</a> professions. The port and shipping industry is well established, with <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_Port" class="mw-redirect" title="Mumbai Port">Mumbai Port</a> being one of the oldest and most significant ports in India.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dharavi" title="Dharavi">Dharavi</a>, in central Mumbai, has an increasingly large recycling industry, processing recyclable waste from other parts of the city; the district has an estimated 15,000 single-room factories.<sup id="cite_ref-gua_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gua-170">[170]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mumbai has been ranked sixth among top ten global cities on the billionaire count,<sup id="cite_ref-timesofindia.indiatimes.com_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timesofindia.indiatimes.com-171">[171]</a></sup> 48th on the <a href="/wiki/Worldwide_Centres_of_Commerce_Index" class="mw-redirect" title="Worldwide Centres of Commerce Index">Worldwide Centres of Commerce Index</a> 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-172">[172]</a></sup> seventh in the list of "Top Ten Cities for Billionaires" by <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> magazine (April 2008),<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> and first in terms of those billionaires' average wealth.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> As of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mumbai&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the Globalization and World Cities Study Group (GaWC) has ranked Mumbai as an "Alpha world city", third in its categories of <a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">Global cities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> Mumbai is the third most expensive office market in the world, and was ranked among the fastest cities in the country for business startup in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Bank_and_International_Financial_Corporation_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Bank_and_International_Financial_Corporation-176">[176]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Civic_administration">Civic administration</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bombay_Municipal_Corporation.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Bombay_Municipal_Corporation.JPG/170px-Bombay_Municipal_Corporation.JPG" width="170" height="254" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Bombay_Municipal_Corporation.JPG/255px-Bombay_Municipal_Corporation.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Bombay_Municipal_Corporation.JPG/340px-Bombay_Municipal_Corporation.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3872" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bombay_Municipal_Corporation.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Municipal_Corporation_of_Greater_Mumbai" class="mw-redirect" title="Municipal Corporation of Greater Mumbai">Municipal Corporation of Greater Mumbai</a> (MCGM). The MCGM is the largest civic organisation in the country.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Greater Mumbai, an area of 603 square kilometres (233&#160;sq&#160;mi),<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> consisting of the <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_City_district" title="Mumbai City district">Mumbai City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_Suburban_district" title="Mumbai Suburban district">Mumbai Suburban</a> districts, extends from <a href="/wiki/Colaba" title="Colaba">Colaba</a> in the south, to <a href="/wiki/Mulund" title="Mulund">Mulund</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dahisar" title="Dahisar">Dahisar</a> in the north, and <a href="/wiki/Mankhurd" title="Mankhurd">Mankhurd</a> in the east. Its population as per the 2011 census was 12,442,373.<sup id="cite_ref-census2011-gtmumcity_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census2011-gtmumcity-178">[178]</a></sup></p>
<p>It is administered by the <a href="/wiki/Municipal_Corporation_of_Greater_Mumbai" class="mw-redirect" title="Municipal Corporation of Greater Mumbai">Municipal Corporation of Greater Mumbai</a> (MCGM) (sometimes referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Brihanmumbai_Municipal_Corporation" title="Brihanmumbai Municipal Corporation">Brihanmumbai Municipal Corporation</a>), formerly known as the <i>Bombay Municipal Corporation</i> (BMC).<sup id="cite_ref-mloc_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mloc-134">[134]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Municipal_Corporation_of_Greater_Mumbai" class="mw-redirect" title="Municipal Corporation of Greater Mumbai">MCGM</a> is in charge of the civic and infrastructure needs of the metropolis.<sup id="cite_ref-mcmmm_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcmmm-179">[179]</a></sup> The Mayor is chosen through indirect election by the councillors from among themselves for a term of two and half years.<sup id="cite_ref-mayorterm_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mayorterm-180">[180]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Municipal Commissioner is the chief Executive Officer and head of the executive arm of the Municipal Corporation. All executive powers are vested in the <a href="/wiki/Municipal_Commissioner_of_Mumbai" title="Municipal Commissioner of Mumbai">Municipal Commissioner</a> who is an <a href="/wiki/Indian_Administrative_Service" title="Indian Administrative Service">Indian Administrative Service</a> (IAS) officer appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Maharashtra#Government" title="Maharashtra">state government</a>. Although the Municipal Corporation is the legislative body that lays down policies for the governance of the city, it is the Commissioner who is responsible for the execution of the policies. The Commissioner is appointed for a fixed term as defined by state statute. The powers of the Commissioner are those provided by statute and those delegated by the Corporation or the Standing Committee.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Municipal Corporation of Greater Mumbai was ranked 9th out of 21 Cities for best governance &amp; administrative practices in India in 2014. It scored 3.5 on 10 compared to the national average of 3.3.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mumbai_03-2016_41_Bombay_High_Court.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A brown building with a central tower and sloping roofs surrounded by trees. A grassy ground and a coconut tree are in front of it." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Mumbai_03-2016_41_Bombay_High_Court.jpg/220px-Mumbai_03-2016_41_Bombay_High_Court.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Mumbai_03-2016_41_Bombay_High_Court.jpg/330px-Mumbai_03-2016_41_Bombay_High_Court.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Mumbai_03-2016_41_Bombay_High_Court.jpg/440px-Mumbai_03-2016_41_Bombay_High_Court.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5098" data-file-height="2868" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mumbai_03-2016_41_Bombay_High_Court.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Bombay_High_Court" class="mw-redirect" title="Bombay High Court">Bombay High Court</a> exercises jurisdiction over Maharashtra, <a href="/wiki/Goa" title="Goa">Goa</a>, Daman and Diu, and <a href="/wiki/Dadra_and_Nagar_Haveli" title="Dadra and Nagar Haveli">Dadra and Nagar Haveli</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The two revenue districts of Mumbai come under the jurisdiction of a <a href="/wiki/District_Collector" class="mw-redirect" title="District Collector">District Collector</a>. The Collectors are in charge of property records and revenue collection for the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India" title="Government of India">Central Government</a>, and oversee the national elections held in the city.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_Police" title="Mumbai Police">Mumbai Police</a> is headed by a <a href="/wiki/Police_Commissioner_of_Mumbai" title="Police Commissioner of Mumbai">Police Commissioner</a>, who is an <a href="/wiki/Indian_Police_Service" title="Indian Police Service">Indian Police Service</a> (IPS) officer. The Mumbai Police is a division of the <a href="/wiki/Maharashtra_Police" title="Maharashtra Police">Maharashtra Police</a>, under the state Home Ministry.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> The city is divided into seven police zones and seventeen <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_traffic_police" class="mw-redirect" title="Mumbai traffic police">traffic police</a> zones,<sup id="cite_ref-trf_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trf-132">[132]</a></sup> each headed by a Deputy Commissioner of Police.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> The Traffic Police is a semi-autonomous body under the Mumbai Police. The <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_Fire_Brigade" title="Mumbai Fire Brigade">Mumbai Fire Brigade</a>, under the jurisdiction of the Municipal Corporation, is headed by the Chief Fire Officer, who is assisted by four Deputy Chief Fire Officers and six Divisional Officers.<sup id="cite_ref-trf_132-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trf-132">[132]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_Metropolitan_Region_Development_Authority" title="Mumbai Metropolitan Region Development Authority">Mumbai Metropolitan Region Development Authority</a> (MMRDA) is responsible for infrastructure development and planning of <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_Metropolitan_Region" title="Mumbai Metropolitan Region">Mumbai Metropolitan Region</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mumbai is the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Bombay_High_Court" class="mw-redirect" title="Bombay High Court">Bombay High Court</a>, which exercises jurisdiction over the states of Maharashtra and <a href="/wiki/Goa" title="Goa">Goa</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Union_Territory" class="mw-redirect" title="Union Territory">Union Territories</a> of <a href="/wiki/Daman_and_Diu" title="Daman and Diu">Daman and Diu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dadra_and_Nagar_Haveli" title="Dadra and Nagar Haveli">Dadra and Nagar Haveli</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> Mumbai also has two lower courts, the <a href="/wiki/Small_Causes_Court" class="mw-redirect" title="Small Causes Court">Small Causes Court</a> for civil matters, and the <a href="/wiki/Sessions_Court" title="Sessions Court">Sessions Court</a> for criminal cases. Mumbai also has a special Terrorist and Disruptive Activities (TADA) court for people accused of conspiring and abetting acts of terrorism in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1st_INC1885.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Men in traditional Indian dresses posing for a photograph" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/1st_INC1885.jpg/220px-1st_INC1885.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/1st_INC1885.jpg/330px-1st_INC1885.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/1st_INC1885.jpg/440px-1st_INC1885.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1060" data-file-height="696" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1st_INC1885.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
First session of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_National_Congress" title="Indian National Congress">Indian National Congress</a> in Bombay (28–31 December 1885)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Mumbai had been a traditional stronghold and birthplace of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_National_Congress" title="Indian National Congress">Indian National Congress</a>, also known as the Congress Party.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> The first session of the Indian National Congress was held in Bombay from 28–31 December 1885.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> The city played host to the Indian National Congress six times during its first 50 years, and became a strong base for the <a href="/wiki/Indian_independence_movement" title="Indian independence movement">Indian independence movement</a> during the 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup></p>
<p>The 1960s saw the rise of regionalist politics in Bombay, with the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Shiv_Sena" title="Shiv Sena">Shiv Sena</a> on 19 June 1966, out of a feeling of resentment about the relative marginalisation of the native <a href="/wiki/Marathi_people" title="Marathi people">Marathi people</a> in Bombay.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> Shiv Sena switched from 'Marathi Cause' to larger 'Hindutva Cause' in 1985 and joined hands with <a href="/wiki/Bhartiya_Janata_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Bhartiya Janata Party">Bhartiya Janata Party</a> (BJP) in same year.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> The Congress had dominated the politics of Bombay from independence until the early 1980s, when the Shiv Sena won the 1985 Bombay Municipal Corporation elections.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1989, the <a href="/wiki/Bharatiya_Janata_Party" title="Bharatiya Janata Party">Bharatiya Janata Party</a> (BJP), a major national political party, forged an electoral alliance with the Shiv Sena to dislodge the Congress in the Maharashtra <a href="/wiki/Vidhan_Sabha" title="Vidhan Sabha">Legislative Assembly</a> elections. In 1999, several members left the Congress to form the <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_Congress_Party" title="Nationalist Congress Party">Nationalist Congress Party</a> (NCP) but later allied with the Congress as part of an alliance known as the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Front_(India)" title="Democratic Front (India)">Democratic Front</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> Currently, other parties such as <a href="/wiki/Maharashtra_Navnirman_Sena" title="Maharashtra Navnirman Sena">Maharashtra Navnirman Sena</a> (MNS), <a href="/wiki/Samajwadi_Party" title="Samajwadi Party">Samajwadi Party</a> (SP), <a href="/wiki/Bahujan_Samaj_Party" title="Bahujan Samaj Party">Bahujan Samaj Party</a> (BSP), and several independent candidates also contest elections in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_India" title="Elections in India">Indian national elections</a> held every five years, Mumbai is represented by six parliamentary constituencies: <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_North_(Lok_Sabha_constituency)" title="Mumbai North (Lok Sabha constituency)">North</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_North_West_(Lok_Sabha_constituency)" title="Mumbai North West (Lok Sabha constituency)">North West</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_North_East_(Lok_Sabha_constituency)" title="Mumbai North East (Lok Sabha constituency)">North East</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_North_Central_(Lok_Sabha_constituency)" title="Mumbai North Central (Lok Sabha constituency)">North Central</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_South_Central_(Lok_Sabha_constituency)" title="Mumbai South Central (Lok Sabha constituency)">South Central</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_South_(Lok_Sabha_constituency)" title="Mumbai South (Lok Sabha constituency)">South</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Member_of_parliament,_Lok_Sabha" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of parliament, Lok Sabha">Member of parliament</a> (MP) to the <i><a href="/wiki/Lok_Sabha" title="Lok Sabha">Lok Sabha</a></i>, the lower house of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian Parliament">Indian Parliament</a>, is elected from each of the parliamentary constituencies. In the <a href="/wiki/Indian_general_election,_2014" title="Indian general election, 2014">2014 national elections</a>, all six parliamentary constituencies were won by the BJP and Shiv Sena in alliance, with both parties winning three seats each.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the Maharashtra state assembly elections held every five years, Mumbai is represented by 36 assembly constituencies.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_Legislative_Assembly_(India)" title="Member of the Legislative Assembly (India)">Member of the Legislative Assembly</a> (MLA) to the Maharashtra <i><a href="/wiki/Vidhan_Sabha" title="Vidhan Sabha">Vidhan Sabha</a></i> (Legislative Assembly) is elected from each of the assembly constituencies. In the <a href="/wiki/Maharashtra_Legislative_Assembly_election,_2014" title="Maharashtra Legislative Assembly election, 2014">2014 state assembly elections</a>, out of the 36 assembly constituencies, 15 were won by the BJP, 14 by the Shiv Sena and 5 by the Congress.<sup id="cite_ref-senaMumbaibelongs_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-senaMumbaibelongs-200">[200]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UnderstandingMaha_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UnderstandingMaha-201">[201]</a></sup></p>
<p>Elections are also held every five years to elect corporators to power in the MCGM.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> The Corporation comprises 227 directly elected Councillors representing the <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Mumbai" title="Administrative divisions of Mumbai">24 municipal wards</a>, five nominated Councillors having special knowledge or experience in municipal administration, and a <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Mumbai" title="Mayor of Mumbai">Mayor</a> whose role is mostly ceremonial.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Brihanmumbai_Mahanagar_Palika_election,_2012" title="Brihanmumbai Mahanagar Palika election, 2012">2012 municipal corporation elections</a>, out of the 227 seats, the Shiv Sena-BJP alliance secured 107 seats, holding power with the support of independent candidates in the MCGM, while the Congress-NCP alliance bagged 64 seats.<sup id="cite_ref-civic20102_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-civic20102-206">[206]</a></sup> The tenure of the <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Mumbai" title="Mayor of Mumbai">Mayor</a>, Deputy Mayor, and <a href="/wiki/Municipal_Commissioner_of_Mumbai" title="Municipal Commissioner of Mumbai">Municipal Commissioner</a> is two and a half years.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Bombay4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Bombay4.jpg/200px-Bombay4.jpg" width="200" height="138" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b2/Bombay4.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="207" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_Suburban_Railway" title="Mumbai Suburban Railway">Mumbai Suburban Railway</a> system carries more than 6.99 million commuters on a daily basis. It has the highest passenger density of any urban railway system in the world.</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">

</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Mumbai_03-2016_48_bus_in_Mahim.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Mumbai_03-2016_48_bus_in_Mahim.jpg/200px-Mumbai_03-2016_48_bus_in_Mahim.jpg" width="200" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Mumbai_03-2016_48_bus_in_Mahim.jpg/300px-Mumbai_03-2016_48_bus_in_Mahim.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Mumbai_03-2016_48_bus_in_Mahim.jpg/400px-Mumbai_03-2016_48_bus_in_Mahim.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4500" data-file-height="3000" /></a></div>

</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:PremierPadminiTaxis_gobeirne.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/PremierPadminiTaxis_gobeirne.jpg/200px-PremierPadminiTaxis_gobeirne.jpg" width="200" height="91" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/PremierPadminiTaxis_gobeirne.jpg/300px-PremierPadminiTaxis_gobeirne.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/PremierPadminiTaxis_gobeirne.jpg/400px-PremierPadminiTaxis_gobeirne.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3520" data-file-height="1596" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The black and yellow Premier Padmini Taxis are iconic of Mumbai.</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Mumbai_03-2016_81_Dadar_Beach_view_of_the_SeaLink.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Mumbai_03-2016_81_Dadar_Beach_view_of_the_SeaLink.jpg/200px-Mumbai_03-2016_81_Dadar_Beach_view_of_the_SeaLink.jpg" width="200" height="113" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Mumbai_03-2016_81_Dadar_Beach_view_of_the_SeaLink.jpg/300px-Mumbai_03-2016_81_Dadar_Beach_view_of_the_SeaLink.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Mumbai_03-2016_81_Dadar_Beach_view_of_the_SeaLink.jpg/400px-Mumbai_03-2016_81_Dadar_Beach_view_of_the_SeaLink.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5472" data-file-height="3078" /></a></div>

</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Jawaharlal_Nehru_Trust_Port.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Jawaharlal_Nehru_Trust_Port.jpg/200px-Jawaharlal_Nehru_Trust_Port.jpg" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Jawaharlal_Nehru_Trust_Port.jpg/300px-Jawaharlal_Nehru_Trust_Port.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Jawaharlal_Nehru_Trust_Port.jpg/400px-Jawaharlal_Nehru_Trust_Port.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru_Port_Trust" class="mw-redirect" title="Jawaharlal Nehru Port Trust">Jawaharlal Nehru Port Trust</a> is the busiest port in India</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transport">Public transport</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Public_transport_in_Mumbai" title="Public transport in Mumbai">Public transport in Mumbai</a></div>
<p>Public transport systems in Mumbai include the <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_Suburban_Railway" title="Mumbai Suburban Railway">Mumbai Suburban Railway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_Monorail" title="Mumbai Monorail">Monorail</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_Metro" title="Mumbai Metro">Metro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brihanmumbai_Electric_Supply_and_Transport" title="Brihanmumbai Electric Supply and Transport">Brihanmumbai Electric Supply and Transport</a> (BEST) buses, black-and-yellow meter <a href="/wiki/Taxicabs" class="mw-redirect" title="Taxicabs">taxis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Auto_rickshaw" title="Auto rickshaw">auto rickshaws</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ferries" class="mw-redirect" title="Ferries">ferries</a>. Suburban railway and BEST bus services together accounted for about 88% of the passenger traffic in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-bus44_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bus44-209">[209]</a></sup> Auto rickshaws are allowed to operate only in the suburban areas of Mumbai, while taxis are allowed to operate throughout Mumbai, but generally operate in <a href="/wiki/South_Mumbai" title="South Mumbai">South Mumbai</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autaxi_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autaxi-210">[210]</a></sup> Taxis and rickshaws in Mumbai are required by law to run on <a href="/wiki/Compressed_natural_gas" title="Compressed natural gas">compressed natural gas</a> (CNG),<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> and are a convenient, economical, and easily available means of transport.<sup id="cite_ref-autaxi_210-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autaxi-210">[210]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_Suburban_Railway" title="Mumbai Suburban Railway">Mumbai Suburban Railway</a>, popularly referred to as Locals forms the backbone of the city's transport system.<sup id="cite_ref-Outlook_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Outlook-212">[212]</a></sup> It is operated by the Central Railway and Western Railway zones of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Railways" title="Indian Railways">Indian Railways</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> Mumbai's suburban rail systems carried a total of 6.3&#160;million passengers every day in 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> which is more than half of the Indian Railways daily carrying capacity. Trains are overcrowded during peak hours, with nine-car trains of rated capacity 1,700 passengers, actually carrying around 4,500 passengers at peak hours.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup> The Mumbai rail network is spread at an expanse of 319 route kilometres. 191 rakes (train-sets) of 9 car and 12 car composition are utilised to run a total of 2,226 train services in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_Monorail" title="Mumbai Monorail">Mumbai Monorail</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_Metro" title="Mumbai Metro">Mumbai Metro</a> have been built and are being extended in phases to relieve overcrowding on the existing network. The Monorail opened in early February 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-startMono_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-startMono-217">[217]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Line_1_(Mumbai_Metro)" title="Line 1 (Mumbai Metro)">first line</a> of the Mumbai Metro opened in early June 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-startMetro_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-startMetro-218">[218]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mumbai is the headquarters of two zones of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Railways" title="Indian Railways">Indian Railways</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Central_Railway_(India)" class="mw-redirect" title="Central Railway (India)">Central Railway (CR)</a> headquartered at <a href="/wiki/Chhatrapati_Shivaji_Terminus" title="Chhatrapati Shivaji Terminus">Chhatrapati Shivaji Terminus</a> (formerly Victoria Terminus), and the <a href="/wiki/Western_Railway_(India)" class="mw-redirect" title="Western Railway (India)">Western Railway (WR)</a> headquartered at <a href="/wiki/Churchgate" title="Churchgate">Churchgate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup> Mumbai is also well connected to most parts of India by the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Railways" title="Indian Railways">Indian Railways</a>. Long-distance trains originate from <a href="/wiki/Chhatrapati_Shivaji_Terminus" title="Chhatrapati Shivaji Terminus">Chhatrapati Shivaji Terminus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dadar_railway_station" title="Dadar railway station">Dadar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lokmanya_Tilak_Terminus" class="mw-redirect" title="Lokmanya Tilak Terminus">Lokmanya Tilak Terminus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_Central" class="mw-redirect" title="Mumbai Central">Mumbai Central</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bandra_Terminus" class="mw-redirect" title="Bandra Terminus">Bandra Terminus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andheri_railway_station" title="Andheri railway station">Andheri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Borivali_railway_station" title="Borivali railway station">Borivali</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus">Bus</span></h4>
<p>Mumbai's bus services carried over 5.5 million passengers per day in 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-bus44_209-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bus44-209">[209]</a></sup> which dropped to 2.8 million in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-BESTdip_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BESTdip-221">[221]</a></sup> Public buses run by BEST cover almost all parts of the metropolis, as well as parts of <a href="/wiki/Navi_Mumbai" title="Navi Mumbai">Navi Mumbai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mira-Bhayandar" title="Mira-Bhayandar">Mira-Bhayandar</a> and Thane.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup> The BEST operates a total of 4,608 buses<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup> with CCTV cameras installed, ferrying 4.5&#160;million passengers daily<sup id="cite_ref-bus44_209-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bus44-209">[209]</a></sup> over 390 routes. Its fleet consists of single-decker, double-decker, vestibule, low-floor, disabled-friendly, air-conditioned and <a href="/wiki/Euro_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Euro III">Euro III</a> compliant diesel and <a href="/wiki/Compressed_natural_gas" title="Compressed natural gas">compressed natural gas</a> powered buses.<sup id="cite_ref-bestfleet_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bestfleet-224">[224]</a></sup> BEST introduced air-conditioned buses in 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-timelineBEST_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timelineBEST-225">[225]</a></sup> BEST buses are red in colour, based originally on the <a href="/wiki/Routemaster" title="Routemaster">Routemaster</a> buses of <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-newkiller_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newkiller-226">[226]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Maharashtra_State_Road_Transport_Corporation" title="Maharashtra State Road Transport Corporation">Maharashtra State Road Transport Corporation</a> (MSRTC, also known as ST)<sup id="cite_ref-training_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-training-227">[227]</a></sup> buses provide intercity transport connecting Mumbai with other towns and cities of Maharashtra and nearby states.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Navi_Mumbai_Municipal_Transport" title="Navi Mumbai Municipal Transport">Navi Mumbai Municipal Transport</a> (NMMT) and <a href="/wiki/Thane_Municipal_Transport" title="Thane Municipal Transport">Thane Municipal Transport</a> (TMT) also operate their buses in Mumbai, connecting various nodes of Navi Mumbai and Thane to parts of Mumbai.<sup id="cite_ref-NMMTgain_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NMMTgain-230">[230]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TMTmoolah_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TMTmoolah-231">[231]</a></sup></p>
<p>Buses are generally favoured for commuting short to medium distances, while train fares are more economical for longer distance commutes.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>Mumbai Darshan</i> is a tourist bus service which explores numerous <a href="/wiki/List_of_tourist_attractions_in_Mumbai" title="List of tourist attractions in Mumbai">tourist attractions in Mumbai</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup> Bus Rapid Transit System (BRTS) lanes have been planned throughout Mumbai.<sup id="cite_ref-routetalpdf_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-routetalpdf-234">[234]</a></sup> Though 88% of the city's commuters travel by public transport, Mumbai still continues to struggle with <a href="/wiki/Traffic_congestion" title="Traffic congestion">traffic congestion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup> Mumbai's transport system has been categorised as one of the most congested in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Water">Water</span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Water_transport_in_Mumbai" title="Water transport in Mumbai">Water transport in Mumbai</a> consists of ferries, hovercrafts and catamarans. Services are provided by both government agencies as well as private partners.<sup id="cite_ref-alibauglaunch_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alibauglaunch-237">[237]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hovercraft" title="Hovercraft">Hovercraft</a> services plied briefly in the late 1990s between the <a href="/wiki/Gateway_of_India" title="Gateway of India">Gateway of India</a> and <a href="/wiki/CBD_Belapur" title="CBD Belapur">CBD Belapur</a> in Navi Mumbai. They were subsequently scrapped due to lack of adequate <a href="/wiki/Water_transport_infrastructure" class="mw-redirect" title="Water transport infrastructure">infrastructure</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nmhovercraft_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nmhovercraft-238">[238]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span></h3>
<p>Mumbai is served by <a href="/wiki/National_Highway_3_(India)" title="National Highway 3 (India)">National Highway 3</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Highway_4_(India)" title="National Highway 4 (India)">National Highway 4</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Highway_8_(India)" title="National Highway 8 (India)">National Highway 8</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Highway_17_(India)" title="National Highway 17 (India)">National Highway 17</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_Highway_222_(India)" class="mw-redirect" title="National Highway 222 (India)">National Highway 222</a> of India's <a href="/wiki/National_Highway_(India)" title="National Highway (India)">National Highways system</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Mumbai-Pune_Expressway" class="mw-redirect" title="Mumbai-Pune Expressway">Mumbai-Pune Expressway</a> was the first <a href="/wiki/National_Expressway_(India)" class="mw-redirect" title="National Expressway (India)">expressway</a> built in India.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Freeway_(Mumbai)" title="Eastern Freeway (Mumbai)">Eastern Freeway</a> was opened in 2013. The <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_Nashik_Expressway" title="Mumbai Nashik Expressway">Mumbai Nashik Expressway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mumbai-Vadodara_Expressway" class="mw-redirect" title="Mumbai-Vadodara Expressway">Mumbai-Vadodara Expressway</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup> are under construction. The <a href="/wiki/Bandra-Worli_Sea_Link" class="mw-redirect" title="Bandra-Worli Sea Link">Bandra-Worli Sea Link</a> bridge, along with <a href="/wiki/Mahim_Causeway" title="Mahim Causeway">Mahim Causeway</a>, links the island city to the western suburbs.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup> The three major road arteries of the city are the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Express_Highway" title="Eastern Express Highway">Eastern Express Highway</a> from <a href="/wiki/Sion,_Mumbai" title="Sion, Mumbai">Sion</a> to Thane, the <a href="/wiki/Sion_Panvel_Expressway" class="mw-redirect" title="Sion Panvel Expressway">Sion Panvel Expressway</a> from <a href="/wiki/Sion,_Mumbai" title="Sion, Mumbai">Sion</a> to <a href="/wiki/Panvel" title="Panvel">Panvel</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Western_Express_Highway" title="Western Express Highway">Western Express Highway</a> from <a href="/wiki/Bandra" title="Bandra">Bandra</a> to <a href="/wiki/Dahisar" title="Dahisar">Dahisar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup> Mumbai has approximately 1,900&#160;km (1,181&#160;mi) of roads.<sup id="cite_ref-dnaindia.com_244-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dnaindia.com-244">[244]</a></sup> There are five <a href="/wiki/Toll_plaza" class="mw-redirect" title="Toll plaza">tolled</a> entry points to the city by road.<sup id="cite_ref-gatewaytollfree_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gatewaytollfree-245">[245]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mumbai had about 721,000 private vehicles as of March 2014,<sup id="cite_ref-TOI1_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TOI1-246">[246]</a></sup> 56,459 black and yellow taxis as of 2005<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mumbai&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>,<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup> and 106,000 auto rickshaws, as of May 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mumbai_airport_domestic_departure_terminal_1C_(6).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Mumbai_airport_domestic_departure_terminal_1C_%286%29.JPG/220px-Mumbai_airport_domestic_departure_terminal_1C_%286%29.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Mumbai_airport_domestic_departure_terminal_1C_%286%29.JPG/330px-Mumbai_airport_domestic_departure_terminal_1C_%286%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Mumbai_airport_domestic_departure_terminal_1C_%286%29.JPG/440px-Mumbai_airport_domestic_departure_terminal_1C_%286%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mumbai_airport_domestic_departure_terminal_1C_(6).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Chhatrapati Shivaji International Airport, Mumbai, India</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Chhatrapati_Shivaji_International_Airport" title="Chhatrapati Shivaji International Airport">Chhatrapati Shivaji International Airport</a> (formerly Sahar International Airport) is the main aviation hub in the city and the second busiest airport in India in terms of passenger traffic.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup> It handled 36.6 million passengers and 694,300 tonnes of cargo during FY 2014–2015.<sup id="cite_ref-APA_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-APA-250">[250]</a></sup> An upgrade plan was initiated in 2006, targeted at increasing the capacity of the airport to handle up to 40&#160;million passengers annually<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup> and the new terminal T2 was opened in February 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup></p>
<p>The proposed <a href="/wiki/Navi_Mumbai_International_airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Navi Mumbai International airport">Navi Mumbai International Airport</a> to be built in the Kopra-<a href="/wiki/Panvel" title="Panvel">Panvel</a> area has been sanctioned by the Indian Government and will help relieve the increasing traffic burden on the existing airport.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">[253]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Juhu_Aerodrome" title="Juhu Aerodrome">Juhu Aerodrome</a> was India's first airport, and now hosts the <a href="/wiki/Bombay_Flying_Club" title="Bombay Flying Club">Bombay Flying Club</a> and a heliport operated by state-owned <a href="/wiki/Pawan_Hans" title="Pawan Hans">Pawan Hans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">[254]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sea">Sea</span></h3>
<p>Mumbai is served by two major ports, <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_Port_Trust" title="Mumbai Port Trust">Mumbai Port Trust</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru_Port_Trust" class="mw-redirect" title="Jawaharlal Nehru Port Trust">Jawaharlal Nehru Port Trust</a>, which lies just across the creek in <a href="/wiki/Navi_Mumbai" title="Navi Mumbai">Navi Mumbai</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">[255]</a></sup> Mumbai Port has one of the best natural harbours in the world, and has extensive wet and dry dock accommodation facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup> Jawaharlal Nehru Port, commissioned on 26 May 1989, is the busiest and most modern major port in India.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">[257]</a></sup> It handles 55–60% of the country's total containerised cargo.<sup id="cite_ref-pt_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pt-258">[258]</a></sup> Ferries from <a href="/wiki/Ferry_Wharf" title="Ferry Wharf">Ferry Wharf</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mazagaon" title="Mazagaon">Mazagaon</a> allow access to islands near the city.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">[259]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city is also the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Naval_Command" title="Western Naval Command">Western Naval Command</a>, and also an important base for the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Navy" title="Indian Navy">Indian Navy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mloc_134-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mloc-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Utility_services">Utility services</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Mumbai%27s_water_sources" class="mw-redirect" title="Mumbai's water sources">Mumbai's water sources</a></div>
<p>Under colonial rule, tanks were the only source of water in Mumbai, with many localities having been named after them. The <a href="/wiki/Municipal_Corporation_of_Greater_Mumbai" class="mw-redirect" title="Municipal Corporation of Greater Mumbai">MCGM</a> supplies potable water to the city from six lakes,<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">[260]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">[261]</a></sup> most of which comes from the Tulsi and Vihar lakes. The Tansa lake supplies water to the western suburbs and parts of the island city along the Western Railway.<sup id="cite_ref-tansa_262-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tansa-262">[262]</a></sup> The water is filtered at <a href="/wiki/Bhandup" title="Bhandup">Bhandup</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-tansa_262-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tansa-262">[262]</a></sup> which is Asia's largest water filtration plant.<sup id="cite_ref-RTIBhandup_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RTIBhandup-263">[263]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-contamination_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-contamination-264">[264]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">[265]</a></sup> India's first underground water tunnel was completed in Mumbai to supply water to the Bhandup filtration plant.<sup id="cite_ref-firstwatertunnel_266-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-firstwatertunnel-266">[266]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tunnelcomplete_267-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tunnelcomplete-267">[267]</a></sup></p>
<p>About 700 million litres of water, out of a daily supply of 3500&#160;million litres, is lost by way of water thefts, illegal connections and leakages, per day in Mumbai.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup> Almost all of Mumbai's daily refuse of 7,800&#160;metric tonnes, of which 40&#160;metric tonnes is plastic waste,<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">[269]</a></sup> is transported to dumping grounds in <a href="/wiki/Gorai" title="Gorai">Gorai</a> in the northwest, <a href="/wiki/Mulund" title="Mulund">Mulund</a> in the northeast, and to the <a href="/wiki/Deonar_dumping_ground" title="Deonar dumping ground">Deonar dumping ground</a> in the east.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">[270]</a></sup> Sewage treatment is carried out at <a href="/wiki/Worli" title="Worli">Worli</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bandra" title="Bandra">Bandra</a>, and disposed of by two independent marine outfalls of 3.4&#160;km (2.1&#160;mi) and 3.7&#160;km (2.3&#160;mi) at Bandra and Worli respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">[271]</a></sup></p>
<p>Electricity is distributed by the <a href="/wiki/Brihanmumbai_Electric_Supply_and_Transport" title="Brihanmumbai Electric Supply and Transport">Brihanmumbai Electric Supply and Transport</a> (BEST) undertaking in the island city, and by <a href="/wiki/Reliance_Infrastructure" title="Reliance Infrastructure">Reliance Energy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tata_Power" title="Tata Power">Tata Power</a>, and the Maharashtra State Electricity Distribution Co. Ltd (<a href="/wiki/Mahavitaran" class="mw-redirect" title="Mahavitaran">Mahavitaran</a>) in the suburbs.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">[272]</a></sup> Consumption of electricity is growing faster than production capacity.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">[273]</a></sup> Power supply cables are <a href="/wiki/Undergrounding" title="Undergrounding">underground</a>, which reduces pilferage, thefts and other losses.<sup id="cite_ref-curbtheft_274-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-curbtheft-274">[274]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-explorecurbtheft_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-explorecurbtheft-275">[275]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cooking gas is supplied in the form of <a href="/wiki/Liquefied_petroleum_gas" title="Liquefied petroleum gas">liquefied petroleum gas cylinders</a> sold by state-owned oil companies,<sup id="cite_ref-cylinderatpump_276-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cylinderatpump-276">[276]</a></sup> as well as through <a href="/wiki/Liquefied_natural_gas" title="Liquefied natural gas">piped natural gas</a> supplied by Mahanagar Gas Limited.<sup id="cite_ref-pipedattractive_277-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pipedattractive-277">[277]</a></sup></p>
<p>The largest telephone service provider is the state-owned <a href="/wiki/MTNL" class="mw-redirect" title="MTNL">MTNL</a>, which held a monopoly over fixed line and cellular services up until 2000, and provides fixed line as well as mobile <a href="/wiki/Wireless_local_loop" title="Wireless local loop">WLL</a> services.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">[278]</a></sup> Mobile phone coverage is extensive, and the main service providers are <a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Essar" class="mw-redirect" title="Vodafone Essar">Vodafone Essar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bharti_Airtel" title="Bharti Airtel">Airtel</a>, MTNL, <a href="/wiki/Loop_Mobile" title="Loop Mobile">Loop Mobile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reliance_Communications" title="Reliance Communications">Reliance Communications</a>, <a href="/wiki/Idea_Cellular" title="Idea Cellular">Idea Cellular</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tata_Indicom" class="mw-redirect" title="Tata Indicom">Tata Indicom</a>. Both <a href="/wiki/GSM" title="GSM">GSM</a> and <a href="/wiki/CDMA" class="mw-redirect" title="CDMA">CDMA</a> services are available in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">[279]</a></sup> Mumbai, along with the area served by <a href="/wiki/Telephone_exchange" title="Telephone exchange">telephone exchanges</a> in <a href="/wiki/Navi_Mumbai" title="Navi Mumbai">Navi Mumbai</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kalyan" title="Kalyan">Kalyan</a> is classified as a <i>Metro</i> telecom circle.<sup id="cite_ref-unifiedLicence_280-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unifiedLicence-280">[280]</a></sup> Many of the above service providers also provide broadband internet and wireless internet access in Mumbai. As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mumbai&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Mumbai had the highest number of internet users in India with 16.4 million users.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">[281]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Heritage_structures_in_Mumbai" title="Heritage structures in Mumbai">Heritage structures in Mumbai</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mumbai_Night_City_(18219784390).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Mumbai_Night_City_%2818219784390%29.jpg/220px-Mumbai_Night_City_%2818219784390%29.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Mumbai_Night_City_%2818219784390%29.jpg/330px-Mumbai_Night_City_%2818219784390%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Mumbai_Night_City_%2818219784390%29.jpg/440px-Mumbai_Night_City_%2818219784390%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5456" data-file-height="3632" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mumbai_Night_City_(18219784390).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mumbai city at night</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:445px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1A%3DDowntownBombay.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/33/1A%3DDowntownBombay.jpg" width="443" height="146" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="443" data-file-height="146" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1A%3DDowntownBombay.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mumbai city skyline</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The architecture of the city is a blend of <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival" class="mw-redirect" title="Gothic Revival">Gothic Revival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indo-Saracenic" class="mw-redirect" title="Indo-Saracenic">Indo-Saracenic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Art_Deco" title="Art Deco">Art Deco</a>, and other contemporary styles. Most of the buildings during the British period, such as the <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Terminus" class="mw-redirect" title="Victoria Terminus">Victoria Terminus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bombay_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Bombay University">Bombay University</a>, were built in Gothic Revival style.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">[282]</a></sup> Their architectural features include a variety of European influences such as German gables, Dutch roofs, Swiss timbering, Romance arches, Tudor casements, and traditional Indian features.<sup id="cite_ref-Profile_283-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Profile-283">[283]</a></sup> There are also a few Indo-Saracenic styled buildings such as the <a href="/wiki/Gateway_of_India" title="Gateway of India">Gateway of India</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">[284]</a></sup> Art Deco styled landmarks can be found along the <a href="/wiki/Marine_Drive,_Mumbai" title="Marine Drive, Mumbai">Marine Drive</a> and west of the <a href="/wiki/Oval_Maidan" title="Oval Maidan">Oval Maidan</a>. Mumbai has the second largest number of Art Deco buildings in the world after <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a>. In the newer suburbs, modern buildings dominate the landscape. Mumbai has by far the largest number of skyscrapers in India, with 956 existing buildings and 272 under construction as of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mumbai&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.</p>
<p>The Mumbai Heritage Conservation Committee (MHCC), established in 1995, formulates special regulations and by-laws to assist in the conservation of the city's heritage structures. Mumbai has two <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Sites" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Sites">UNESCO World Heritage Sites</a>, the Chhatrapati Shivaji Terminus and the <a href="/wiki/Elephanta_Caves" title="Elephanta Caves">Elephanta Caves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">[285]</a></sup> In the south of Mumbai, there are colonial-era buildings and Soviet-style offices.<sup id="cite_ref-economist_286-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economist-286">[286]</a></sup> In the east are factories and some slums. On the West coast are former-textile mills being demolished and skyscrapers built on top. There are 31 buildings taller than 100&#160;m, compared with 200 in Shanghai, 500 in Hong Kong and 500 in New York.<sup id="cite_ref-economist_286-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economist-286">[286]</a></sup></p>
<div class="center">
<div class="thumb tnone">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:652px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Victoria_Terminus,_Mumbai.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A brown building with clock towers, domes and pyramidal tops. Also a busiest railway station in India.[287] A wide street in front of it" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Victoria_Terminus%2C_Mumbai.jpg/650px-Victoria_Terminus%2C_Mumbai.jpg" width="650" height="251" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/86/Victoria_Terminus%2C_Mumbai.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="972" data-file-height="375" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Victoria_Terminus,_Mumbai.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Chhatrapati_Shivaji_Terminus" title="Chhatrapati Shivaji Terminus">Chhatrapati Shivaji Terminus</a>, formerly known as Victoria Terminus, is the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Railway_(India)" class="mw-redirect" title="Central Railway (India)">Central Railway</a> and a UNESCO <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Growth_of_Mumbai" title="Growth of Mumbai">Growth of Mumbai</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_statistics" title="Mumbai statistics">Mumbai statistics</a></div>

<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/2011_census_of_India" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 census of India">2011 census</a>, the population of Mumbai city was 12,479,608. The population density is estimated to be about 20,482 persons per square kilometre. The living space is 4.5sq metre per person.<sup id="cite_ref-mmmumbaiproperty_289-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mmmumbaiproperty-289">[289]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_Metropolitan_Region" title="Mumbai Metropolitan Region">Mumbai Metropolitan Region</a> was home to 20,748,395 people by 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-extended_UA_2011_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-extended_UA_2011-9">[9]</a></sup> As Per 2011 census, Greater Mumbai, the area under the administration of the <a href="/wiki/MCGM" class="mw-redirect" title="MCGM">MCGM</a>, has a literacy rate of 94.7%, higher than the national average of 86.7%. The number of slum-dwellers is estimated to be 9 million, up from 6 million in 2001,<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">[290]</a></sup> that is, 62% of all Mumbaikars live in informal slums.</p>
<p>The sex ratio in 2011 was 838 females per 1,000 males in the island city, 857 in the suburbs, and 848 as a whole in Greater Mumbai, all numbers lower than the national average of 914 females per 1,000 males. The low sex ratio is partly because of the large number of male migrants who come to the city to work.<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">[291]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Parsis3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Parsis3.jpg/220px-Parsis3.jpg" width="220" height="305" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Parsis3.jpg/330px-Parsis3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Parsis3.jpg/440px-Parsis3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="537" data-file-height="745" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Parsis3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
"<i>Parsis of Bombay</i>", a wood engraving, <i>ca.</i> 1878. Mumbai is home to the largest population of <a href="/wiki/Parsi" title="Parsi">Parsis</a> in the world.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Residents of Mumbai call themselves <i><a href="/wiki/Mumbaikar" class="mw-redirect" title="Mumbaikar">Mumbaikar</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-Mumbaikar_292-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mumbaikar-292">[292]</a></sup> <i>Mumbaiite</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-Mumbaiite_293-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mumbaiite-293">[293]</a></sup> <i>Bombayite</i> or <i>Bombaiite</i>. Mumbai has a large polyglot population like any other <a href="/wiki/Status_of_Indian_cities" class="mw-redirect" title="Status of Indian cities">metropolitan city</a> of India. Sixteen major <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_India" title="Languages of India">languages of India</a> are also spoken in Mumbai, most common being <a href="/wiki/Marathi_language" title="Marathi language">Marathi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hindi_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindi language">Hindi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gujarati_language" title="Gujarati language">Gujarati</a> and English.<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">[294]</a></sup> English is extensively spoken and is the principal language of the city's <a href="/wiki/White-collar_worker" title="White-collar worker">white collar</a> workforce. A colloquial form of Hindi, known as <i><a href="/wiki/Bambaiya" class="mw-redirect" title="Bambaiya">Bambaiya</a></i> – a blend of Marathi, <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gujarati_language" title="Gujarati language">Gujarati</a>, <a href="/wiki/Konkani" class="mw-redirect" title="Konkani">Konkani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">Urdu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indian_English" title="Indian English">Indian English</a> and some invented words – is spoken on the streets.<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">[295]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mumbai suffers from the same major urbanisation problems seen in many fast growing cities in <a href="/wiki/Developing_countries" class="mw-redirect" title="Developing countries">developing countries</a>: widespread poverty and unemployment, poor public health and poor civic and educational standards for a large section of the population. With available land at a premium, Mumbai residents often reside in cramped, relatively expensive housing, usually far from workplaces, and therefore requiring long commutes on crowded mass transit, or clogged roadways. Many of them live in close proximity to bus or train stations although suburban residents spend significant time travelling southward to the main commercial district.<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">[296]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dharavi" title="Dharavi">Dharavi</a>, Asia's second largest <a href="/wiki/Slum" title="Slum">slum</a> (if <a href="/wiki/Karachi" title="Karachi">Karachi</a>'s Orangi Town is counted as a single slum)<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">[297]</a></sup> is located in central Mumbai and houses between 800,000 and one million people<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">[298]</a></sup> in 2.39 square kilometres (0.92&#160;sq&#160;mi), making it one of the most densely populated areas on Earth<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">[299]</a></sup> with a population density of at least 334,728 persons per square kilometre. With a literacy rate of 69%, the slums in Mumbai are the most literate in India.<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">[300]</a></sup></p>
<p>The number of migrants to Mumbai from outside Maharashtra during the 1991–2001 decade was 1.12&#160;million, which amounted to 54.8% of the net addition to the population of Mumbai.<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">[301]</a></sup></p>
<p>The number of households in Mumbai is forecast to rise from 4.2 million in 2008 to 6.6 million in 2020. The number of households with annual incomes of 2 million rupees will increase from 4% to 10% by 2020, amounting to 660,000 families. The number of households with incomes from 1–2 million rupees is also estimated to increase from 4% to 15% by 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">[302]</a></sup> According to Report of <a href="/wiki/Central_Pollution_Control_Board" title="Central Pollution Control Board">Central Pollution Control Board (CPCB)</a> 2016 Mumbai is the noisiest city in India before <a href="/wiki/Lucknow" title="Lucknow">Lucknow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad" title="Hyderabad">Hyderabad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">[303]</a></sup></p>
